width="auto"><div class="stMarkdown" data-testid="stMarkdown"><div data-testid="stMarkdownContainer" class="st-emotion-cache-1104ytp e1icttdg0"><p>UNIT THREE: ENVIRONMENTAL HEALTH</p>
<p>This unit focuses on the components of environment and their effect on humans, water and sanitation, appropriate methods of handling food, and the effects of housing on health. The final section will focus on how the community nurse should mobilise the community in the control of vectors and pests in their environment. Environmental health is one of the most important aspects of primary prevention of diseases. The community health nurse and all the other health workers have a responsibility to assist their communities to improve their environment.</p>
<p>This unit is composed of five sections:
Section One: Health and the Environment
Section Two: Water and Sanitation
Section Three: Appropriate Methods of Handling Food
Section Four: Housing
Section Five: Control of Vectors and Pests</p>
<p>Unit Objectives</p>
<p>By the end of this unit you will be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Explain the importance of environment to community health</li>
<li>Describe water and sanitation in relation to health</li>
<li>Outline appropriate methods of handling food</li>
<li>Describe the effects of housing on health</li>
<li>Mobilise the community in the control of vectors and pests</li>
</ul>
<p>SECTION 1: HEALTH AND THE ENVIRONMENT</p>
<p>Introduction</p>
<p>Welcome to section one of the Environmental Health unit. Since the environment comprises all things that make up your surroundings, environmental health, therefore, describes the aspects of health related to or emanating from your interaction with the environment.</p>
<p>Objectives</p>
<ul>
<li>Define the environment</li>
<li>Explain the components of the environment</li>
<li>Describe the effects of environmental factors on health</li>
</ul>
<p>Environmental Components and their Effect on your Health</p>
<p>The following factors can have an effect on your health:</p>
<ul>
<li>Biological environment</li>
<li>Physical environment</li>
<li>Socio-cultural environment</li>
<li>Economic and political components of the environment</li>
</ul>
<p>Biological Environment</p>
<p>The biological component of the environment is made up of living things, which include plants, people and animals. The adjacent figure shows some examples of biological components.</p>
<p>Plants</p>
<p>Vegetation prevents soil erosion and also protects our water sources. Trees act as windbreakers, provide firewood, charcoal, timber and paper among others. They also influence weather patterns. Flowers are a natural beauty and are often used for decoration. Plants provide vegetables, fruits, tubers and seeds as food.</p>
<p>A number of plants are used as herbal medicine for the treatment of various diseases, for example, the Neem tree locally known as muarobaine, is used for the treatment of malaria, among many other diseases. Garlic is used to treat hypertension. The aloe vera plant is used for prevention of cancer of the stomach and healing of wounds. On the other hand, some plants may adversely affect health. Occasionally, people react to pollen from blooming plants and may develop hay fever or asthma. Ingesting or touching some poisonous plants may have devastating effects.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 70 of 267
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 71 of 267
Bishop's Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="people">People<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#people" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Human beings and their activities can be a big source of infection. For example, overcrowding and slum settlements brought about by urbanisation, can promote the transmission of diseases, especially those diseases that are spread through droplets and contact.</p>
<p>Explosions from quarries produce a lot of dust, which causes respiratory and eye problems. When it rains, these quarries collect water and become breeding sites for mosquitoes and risky places for children.</p>
<p>The felling of trees provides firewood and charcoal but, at the same time, it destroys the water sources. Cultivating along riverbanks may contaminate the water supply through seepage of the fertilizers and pesticides used on the crops. Overgrazing causes soil erosion, destroys vegetation and contaminates water sources.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="animals">Animals<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#animals" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Domestic animals such as cattle, sheep, goats and poultry provide meat, milk and eggs for consumption. Some of them supply hides and wool for commercial purposes. They also provide manure, which is used to increase food produce. Wildlife is often a tourist attraction and acts as a source of income for our country. Cats and dogs are kept as pets, but they can also transmit diseases such as cat scratch fever and rabies, respectively.</p>
<p>Other hazards include snakebites, which can be fatal and insect bites, which may act as vectors of various diseases. For example, mosquitoes are vectors of malaria, yellow fever and filariasis. Houseflies are vectors of dysentery and other diarrhoeal diseases. Bacteria, rickettsia and fungi are also part of the biological environment and are disease-causing organisms in man.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260116-dd568561.jpeg" alt="img-0.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="physical-environment">Physical Environment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#physical-environment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The physical components of the environment are divided into geographical and man-made components. Land is used for settlements. When the land is fertile and well used, it provides enough food for consumption. On the other hand, when the land is infertile, the food supply will be inadequate, resulting into nutritional problems.</p>
<p>The type of soil, climate and altitude determine the type of crops that can be grown in a specific area. Some crops will do well in a hot climate, others will not. For example, tea, peas and pyrethrum thrive in cool climates. However, cold climates encourage respiratory diseases and joint problems such as arthritis. In hot climates, most legumes and fruits such as oranges and mangoes do well. Diseases associated with hot climates include malaria.</p>
<p>Snakes are also common in hot areas and their bites can be fatal. Some disease outbreaks occur during the rainy season, for example, cholera, typhoid and malaria. Similarly, during dry seasons there may be a shortage of food leading to malnutrition. Persistent crop failure will lead to food insecurity and famine.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260116-2f4c6bd2.jpeg" alt="img-1.jpeg"></p>
<p>Each type of climate has its own pattern of vegetation and animals to control. Man has to adjust to the animals and the vegetation since they affect health. Additionally, to adjust to the different temperatures man has to use appropriate clothing.</p>
<p>Remember:
<strong>Most micro-organisms that cause disease are transmitted through air, water and food.</strong>
Therefore, constructing houses too close to a dam or where animals are kept facilitates the transmission of vector borne diseases. Industrial wastes that consist of chemicals and toxic substances, may also pollute the water, air and food.
Moreover, dampness in houses favours the transmission of airborne diseases.
It is your responsibility as a health worker to identify ways of helping the community to improve their environment. You have to be a role model in your homes, health facilities and also in assisting various community development projects.</p>
<p>How would you define pollution? In what ways do natural resources get polluted?
Pollution is the term used to describe the spoiling of natural resources such as air, food and water by harmful substances. Industrial waste such as smoke can pollute the air and water. Other industrial wastes can pollute the soil and vegetation. In the rural areas, where people are involved in agricultural activities, pollution may result from the use of insecticides, pesticides and industrial waste.
Environmental health problems however are usually more prevalent in towns and slums than in rural areas. As a health worker you can make a difference in the community by assisting individuals, families and the community to make their environment healthy.</p>
<p>Socio-Cultural Environment
The figure on your right illustrates some of the socio-cultural factors that may affect health and health practices.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260116-90b4cd7c.jpeg" alt="img-2.jpeg"></p>
<p>Some of the health issues affected by these factors are food habits and cooking practices. Different communities have different food habits and cooking practices. For example, the Kikuyu community have maize and beans (Githeri) as their staple food whereas the Luo community have a cooked preparation of maize flour (Ugali) as their staple food.
Food taboos also vary from one community to the other. Examples of food taboos include prohibiting pregnant mothers from taking some types of meat, believed to affect the foetus.
Wife inheritance and polygamy practices encouraged by some communities provide an</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>opportunity for spreading sexually transmitted diseases and HIV/AIDS. Tattoos performed for beautification and circumcision are other practices where the procedures may be carried out using unsafe instruments and can easily transmit diseases like HIV/AIDS among others.</p>
<p>Female genital mutilation can lead to difficult deliveries. Some people discourage breastfeeding practice considering it to be primitive. This denies the child all the benefits of breastfeeding. Other people do not make use of the available prenatal and delivery services. This affects the growth of the baby and the health of the mother.</p>
<p>Customs and beliefs have an effect on human health. Identify those beliefs that you think you need to discuss with the community to change and those to uphold. It is important to listen to the community's reasons for their beliefs and practices. This will facilitate the choice of the health measures and suitable solutions after discussion.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="economic-and-political-components-of-the-environment">Economic and Political Components of the Environment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#economic-and-political-components-of-the-environment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>These components include work, money and government. The economic factor relates to both rural and urban economies as well as local community organisation. Rural and urban economics will determine to a great extent the quality of environmental health. People can change their environment either positively or negatively. Some of these changes are described as development.</p>
<p>Some development projects may make the environment healthier, while others make it a suitable habitat for diseases. An example is that of irrigation schemes for growing rice, which is a cash crop. This improves the peoples' income, but at the same time, rice fields are breeding sites of mosquitoes and snails, which are vectors of malaria and schistosomiasis respectively.</p>
<p>Other examples of the relation between health and economic status abound. People of low economic status may resort to drinking as a way of relieving their stress. This is usually at the expense of the family budget for basic needs and may lead to health problems. The rich also may suffer from diseases of life style such as obesity, gout, and hypertension among others. The government involves political influences into</p>
<p>development policies.</p>
<p>Think of leadership in the catchment area of your health facility. List three examples of health activities that have been affected by leadership at their implementation stage.</p>
<p>From your experience, relate how leadership influences the implementation of health activities. Your answer should include health activities such as home visiting, school health services, outreach services and local development projects. This gives you insight into the role leadership plays in health care delivery services</p>
<p>The government develops policies, which enforce environmental health. It also plays a great part in influencing the implementation of health activities. Political instability causes unrest, insecurity and psychological problems. Management of disease outbreaks may be lacking as health facilities may be destroyed.</p>
<p>You have now understood the influence the economic and political component of the environment can have on health. You need to identify yourself with local community organisations in your area and work in cooperation with the government officials at various levels. This will facilitate the implementation of various health activities successfully.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="section-2-water-and-sanitation">SECTION 2: WATER AND SANITATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-2-water-and-sanitation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>The section is divided into three sub-sections. In the first one, you will look at water, identifying various water related diseases as well as sources of water, water contamination and the purification of water. In the second sub-section you will examine types of waste and finally, in the last sub-section, you will study methods of waste disposal.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="objectives">Objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>By the end of this section you will be able to:</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>Describe the importance of water in relation to health</li>
<li>Explain different types of waste</li>
<li>Describe various methods of waste disposal</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="water">Water<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#water" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Water is essential for life. It is found in every cell in our body and is necessary for most basic functions, like respiration, digestion and other chemical processes. More than 50% of human body weight is made up of water. Water is thus vital to health and survival but it may itself become the source of diseases, therefore, it should be properly treated and made safe for domestic use.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-role-does-water-play-in-the-transmission-of-the-following-diseases">What role does water play in the transmission of the following diseases?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-role-does-water-play-in-the-transmission-of-the-following-diseases" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Scabies</li>
<li>Cholera</li>
<li>Schistosomiasis</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="role-played-by-water-on-the-transmission-of-diseases">Role Played by Water on the Transmission of Diseases<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#role-played-by-water-on-the-transmission-of-diseases" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Water may contribute to the spread of diseases in several ways. When there is not enough water, and people cannot observe basic personal hygiene, diseases like scabies, non-specific diarrhoeas, dysentery and trachoma spread. Such diseases whose spread is promoted by lack of adequate water are called water-washed (water scarce) diseases. Simply improving the quantity of water can prevent them.</p>
<p>Water can also contribute to the spread of diseases when it carries a specific disease-causing organism. Examples are typhoid, cholera, amoebiasis, hepatitis A, or poliomyelitis. Such diseases caused by contaminated water are called water-borne diseases, and the only way to prevent them is to improve the quality that is, the cleanliness of the water.</p>
<p>Finally, water can contribute to the spread of disease when it is necessary in the life cycle of a disease vector, for example malaria and schitosomomiasis. These diseases are called water-related diseases. Other water related diseases include: onchocerciasis (river blindness) and dracunculosis (guinea worm).</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260116-7e813a6c.jpeg" alt="img-3.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="uses-of-water">Uses of Water<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#uses-of-water" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Water is used in various ways. These include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Human consumption for body needs</li>
<li>Animal watering</li>
<li>Industrial use for manufacturing</li>
<li>For recreational activities such as swimming</li>
<li>To produce electricity</li>
<li>Sustaining of aquatic life, for example, fish for consumption and export</li>
<li>Household purposes like washing and cooking</li>
</ul>
<p>Simple improvements at the community level are required to ensure adequate quality and quantity of water.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sources-of-water">Sources of Water<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sources-of-water" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Water does not stay in one place for very long - it goes round in a cycle. It evaporates from seas and lakes and falls back to the earth as rain. After rainfall, some of the water evaporates and the rest is drained into streams, rivers, lakes and ponds.</p>
<p>The most important water for a community is the water that is held in the soil, by the roots of the trees in the forest. This is a community's long-term underground water store. This is why it is important for you to educate the community on the need to preserve their forests.</p>
<p>There are four main sources of water namely rain water, surface water, underground water and sea water.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="rain-water">Rain Water<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#rain-water" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>This water is relatively pure and clean. Its state of cleanliness depends on levels of atmospheric pollution and how it is collected. The cleanest natural water available is that which is collected from iron sheets into gutters and led by pipes into clean closed tanks. When the first rainwater falls, the last part of the gutters leading to the tank should be removed for some time to ensure that dirt on the roof does not enter the tank. One disadvantage of this water source is that it is difficult to collect from thatched roofs.</p>
<p>The community health nurse can assist the community members to ensure collection of clean water.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="surface-water">Surface Water<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#surface-water" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This type of water includes shallow springs and shallow wells, streams, rivers, dams, ponds and lakes.</p>
<p>A spring is a natural issue of underground water. When the rainwater falls on the surface it sinks into the ground until it reaches the impermeable layer of rock, which it cannot go through.</p>
<p>All the water above this layer is called surface water. If it finds a point of issue it is called a shallow spring. If a well is dug into it, it is called a shallow well, despite its depth. The quantity of water yielded by shallow springs or wells varies according to the season. They may dry up during droughts and are liable to contamination by latrines.</p>
<p>A river is a large mass of flowing water. During the rainy season, its waters become turbid, while in the dry season they are clear.</p>
<p>River water has a lot of impurities obtained from human and animal waste, washing, sewage, agricultural waste and industrial waste.</p>
<p>Other sources of water are dams, ponds and lakes. All these sources provide fresh water.</p>
<p>Remember you have fresh water lakes in this country, which includes Lake Victoria, Lake Baringo, Lake Turkana and Lake Naivasha. However, the water from these sources is often unclean and not safe for drinking. It is therefore important to identify suitable ways of rendering it safe.</p>
<p>The quality of water depends on the location of its sources. If the water source is from the forest, hills and valleys, it is clean and suitable for household use with little or no prior treatment.</p>
<p>This is because there is no human settlement, which might be a source of potential pollutants, at or around the water source.</p>
<p>On the other hand, streams, rivers and lakes around or within towns and villages are likely to be contaminated by human and animal waste. It is, therefore, important to protect water sources from human settlement or animal grazing.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sea-water">Sea Water<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sea-water" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This water is salty and requires expensive purification processes to make it suitable for drinking. In your country you have several salty lakes, which are Lake Magadi, Lake Bogoria and Lake Elementaita. There are also the salty waters of the Indian Ocean.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="underground-water">Underground Water<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#underground-water" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The water that gets under the impermeable layer of rock is called underground water. It is the water between two impermeable layers of rock, one above and the other one below. This water finds an outlet through a fissure or crack in the upper layer of the rock. Water from this issue is obtained as a deep spring, a well or a borehole.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sources-of-water-contamination">Sources of Water Contamination<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sources-of-water-contamination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Water has the ability to absorb substances and gases, for example, oxygen and carbon dioxide as it falls as rain. It also absorbs minerals, for example, different salts from rocks or even dangerous chemicals from industrial wastes.</p>
<p>Collecting surfaces for rainwater may have leaves, insects, bird droppings and animal faeces on them. When water runs over the earth it may become contaminated with human or animal excreta, refuse, fertilizers or industrial wastes.</p>
<p>Excreta and refuse may contaminate shallow wells. Wells may also be contaminated by the use of dirty containers for drawing water or by oil from a pump. Bathing, urinating, defecating in water, washing clothes and animal watering may contaminate rivers, lakes or dams.</p>
<p>Even piped water may become contaminated from leaks in the pipes, especially when they pass near dirty drains or when it is collected in contaminated containers. Water may go bad if it</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>is uncovered or stored for too long in a pot or cistern. Finally, it is important to remember that water from any source may become contaminated if it is drunk from dirty or communal drinking vessels.</p>
<p><strong>Remember:</strong>
It is easier to prevent water from getting dirty than it is to clean it.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="protection-of-water-sources">Protection of Water Sources<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#protection-of-water-sources" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Water sources are precious and must be kept free from contamination.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="rain-water">Rain Water<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#rain-water" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The protection of rainwater sources is done by the use of gutters led by pipes into a small waste drain tank and into a clean closed tank. As you have seen earlier, the first rainwater cleans the roof and the last part of the gutter should be disconnected to render the water clean.</p>
<p>You can identify the need to discuss with the community simple methods of water protection during home visits.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="surface-water">Surface Water<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#surface-water" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>To protect surface water, people should not settle around springs, streams and rivers. People and animals should be kept away from water catchments areas, normally in the forest or up the hills.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="springs">Springs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#springs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Clear the bush or long grass around the site of the spring.</li>
<li>Put up a fence around the spring to prevent animals from grazing and children from playing around it.</li>
<li>Dig a drain about 15 metres from the spring to divert surface water.</li>
<li>Build a strong retaining wall around the 'eyes' point from which water flows out from underground. This wall holds water from the 'eyes' of the spring.</li>
<li>Fix the delivery pipe at a height close to the level of the 'eye' but high enough to allow the water containers to stand below the pipe.</li>
<li>Build steps to the spring as well as a platform on which to place the</li>
</ul>
<p>containers when collecting waters. The area behind the retaining wall should prevent contamination without interfering with the water flow.</p>
<ul>
<li>Design an area for washing and for watering the animals.</li>
<li>Select a caretaker to maintain the protected springs.</li>
</ul>
<p>With this knowledge, you will be able to work with the public health technician or officer in protecting water sources in the catchment area of your health facility.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="wells">Wells<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#wells" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The site should be selected at least 100 metres from a pit latrine or other likely source of contamination.</li>
<li>The sides of the well should be built with stones, rocks, or cement culvert.</li>
<li>The sides above the surrounding ground should be constructed with a sloping water-proof area to avoid dirt from getting into to the well.</li>
<li>A strong well cover should be put in place.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Remember:</strong>
The well should be dug during the dry season to obtain adequate depth, filtration and constant water supply.</p>
<p>The community health nurse and community members should identify practical methods for protecting the water sources in the community. The public health technician or officer can offer technical knowledge on silting of springs and wells.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="purification-of-water-sources">Purification of Water Sources<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#purification-of-water-sources" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Chemicals can be used to purify water sources. Iodine is a disinfecting agent used as 2% tincture. Two drops are sufficient to disinfect one litre of water. Iodine tablets such as GlobalineÂ® and Potable AquaÂ® (trade names) are also used in the sterilisation of small amounts of water as directed by the manufacturer.</p>
<p>After the treatment of water, it is important to store the water safely to prevent recontamination. A safe storage container is a narrow mouthed container that has a lid. The drinking water should not be removed from its</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>container by dipping a potentially contaminated vessel. Instead, it should be poured out of the container or the container should be fitted with a tap.</p>
<p>The community should be educated on simple and practical ways of protecting their water such as the safe water system.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="safe-water-system">Safe Water System<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#safe-water-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The safe water system is a household-based water quality intervention in response to the need for inexpensive, alternative means of water treatment and storage in the short to medium terms. The intervention has three components:</p>
<ul>
<li>Water treatment in the home</li>
<li>Safe storage</li>
<li>Behaviour change techniques</li>
</ul>
<p>The main goals of safe water systems are:</p>
<ul>
<li>To improve the microbial quality of water in the home by means of sustainable technology</li>
<li>To reduce morbidity and mortality of diarrhoea diseases related to contaminated water</li>
<li>To improve hygienic behaviour related to water use</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="chlorination">Chlorination<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chlorination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Chlorine is added to water that has been filtered on a large-scale for supply in cities and towns. Chlorination is the final safeguard of the quality of water.</p>
<p>The amount of chlorine added to the water should be proportioned to the volume of flow and to the chlorine demand of water. Chlorine should be properly mixed and there should be a minimum contact period of 30 minutes, for it to be effective against pathogenic organisms in water.</p>
<p>For household use, 1% of chlorine is recommended. This is normally in the form of JikÂ®, MiltonÂ® or Water GuardÂ® which are trade names. Chlorine should be properly mixed and there should be a minimum contact period of 30 minutes.</p>
<p>some of the ways in which you can sterilise water.</p>
<p>Klorinâ„¢/Waterguardâ„¢ and Clay Pot</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260116-903bfc32.jpeg" alt="img-4.jpeg">
Klorin Waterguard</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260116-1c61e9dd.jpeg" alt="img-5.jpeg">
Clay Pot</p>
<p>Two drops to a litre of water will adequately sterilise the water.</p>
<p>Jerry Cans and Modified Clay Pot</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260116-323a3bd3.jpeg" alt="img-6.jpeg">
Jerry Can</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260116-ceb2b0a7.jpeg" alt="img-7.jpeg">
Modified Clay Pot</p>
<p>Protect purified water by keeping it in suitable water vessels.</p>
<p><strong>Remember:</strong></p>
<p>To treat water using these chemicals read the manufacturer's instructions carefully.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sanitation">Sanitation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sanitation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="types-of-waste">Types of Waste<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-waste" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>You are now going to turn your attention to different types of waste. Man produces waste wherever he is and it is necessary to manage this waste properly to prevent diseases.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="what-are-some-of-the-types-of-waste-that-you-know-of">What are some of the types of waste that you know of?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-are-some-of-the-types-of-waste-that-you-know-of" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>There are two types of waste: solid and liquid. Liquid waste includes excreta and wastewater. Solid waste is also known as refuse.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="liquid-waste">Liquid Waste<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#liquid-waste" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Human excreta are faeces and urine. They are a source of pathogenic organisms.</p>
<p>Excreta are offensive to both sight and smell and can also lead to the contamination of water and foods. Faecal organisms may infect people directly or indirectly through an intermediate host. Human excreta may spread the following diseases:</p>
<ul>
<li>Typhoid fever</li>
<li>Cholera</li>
<li>Intestinal worms</li>
<li>Poliomyelitis</li>
<li>Infective hepatitis A</li>
<li>Bacillary and amoebic dysentery</li>
</ul>
<p>Urine carries the infective ova of schistosoma heamatobium while faeces spread the schistosoma mansoni.</p>
<p>Faeces should not be accessible to fingers, feet, flies and food. The fingers and flies transfer the faeces to the food through the faecal-oral route transmission, known as the 4F connection, which is illustrated in the adjacent figure.</p>
<p>It is, therefore, necessary to help people understand the importance of proper excreta disposal by use of simple and cheap facilities.</p>
<p>As a nurse, you should be able to identify possible customs and beliefs, which hinder proper excreta disposal in the community and educate the people accordingly.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260116-c041af71.jpeg" alt="img-8.jpeg">
The 4F Connection</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="solid-waste">Solid Waste<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#solid-waste" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Solid waste or refuse is defined as any unwanted discarded material, the remains, residual or by-products of human activities which are no longer required for further use by the initial producer. This is normally in the process of:</p>
<ul>
<li>Preparation</li>
<li>Manufacture</li>
<li>Packing</li>
<li>Other human related activities</li>
</ul>
<p>If solid waste is not disposed of properly, it may create a number of problems:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>It may produce an offensive smell</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It attracts insects, vectors/pests particularly flies, cockroaches and rats</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Spreads diseases</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It can cause pollution of air, water or food</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It can cause accidents, for example, fires, cuts and falls</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>There are various sources of solid waste. These include domestic waste, street waste, industrial waste, hospital objectionable waste and garden/agricultural waste. Now look at each of these sources in more detail.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="different-types-of-waste">different types of waste.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#different-types-of-waste" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="domestic-waste">Domestic Waste<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#domestic-waste" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This usually consists of all the garbage that emanates from inside a house, for example, food leftovers, potato and banana peelings, waste paper, worn out clothes, shoes, broken utensils, bottles and tins.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="street-waste">Street Waste<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#street-waste" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This type of refuse consists of paper, food and commercial refuse in public places such as markets and hotels.</p>
<p>Scrap metals may also be included in this category.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="industrial-waste">Industrial Waste<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#industrial-waste" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This varies with the type of industry. Modern industries produce chemical wastes, which are potentially hazardous to man and other living things. The wastes may be toxic, caustic, acidic or flammable. This means that they need special disposal. If the chemical waste is to be discharged into a stream it should be processed first. If it is solid, it should not be dumped on land as it may eventually seep underground and contaminate water sources.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="hospital-waste">Hospital Waste<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hospital-waste" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is the most familiar waste that nurses are aware of. It includes the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>Sharps, that is, needles and syringes</li>
<li>Gauze and cotton wool swabs</li>
<li>Vials and Lotions</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>Drugs and vaccines</li>
<li>Tubing, gloves and papers</li>
<li>Foetuses</li>
</ul>
<p>Health workers have the responsibility of maintaining infection prevention by proper decontamination and disposal of the above waste.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="garden-agricultural-waste">Garden/Agricultural Waste<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#garden-agricultural-waste" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Agricultural waste from coffee, sugarcane, sisal, pesticides and fertilizers may result in the pollution of natural resources such as air, food, and water.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="waste-disposal">Waste Disposal<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#waste-disposal" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You will now look at various methods of waste disposal, covering the disposal of both liquid and solid wastes.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="liquid-waste-disposal">Liquid Waste Disposal<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#liquid-waste-disposal" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The best method of excreta disposal in rural areas is a pit latrine, while toilets are suitable for urban areas. As a health worker, it is important for you to know how a pit latrine is constructed. There are some general guidelines that should be considered when choosing the site for a pit latrine to ensure that water sources among others are not contaminated.</p>
<p>Some of these guidelines are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Pit latrines and cesspools should be at least two to three metres respectively above the water table</li>
<li>Latrines should be located at least six metres away from the buildings</li>
<li>Wells should be located upstream to avoid contamination of the well by ground water passing through the pit latrine or cesspool</li>
</ul>
<p>The excreta disposal system is divided into two categories. These are: water carriage system and non-water carriage system.</p>
<p>In the water carriage system, excreta are disposed by the use of a flush toilet, which is also called a water closet. The flush toilet is the most permanent and hygienic method of excreta disposal. This system is used where there is a permanent, continuous and adequate piped water supply system. This is mainly in cities and towns.</p>
<p>Water closets are reliable and convenient for any permanent building. The excreta are carried by water pressure into a septic tank or sewage pit. The clear fluid effluent needs further</p>
<p>bacteriological treatment to become inactive. It is then led over stones and sand in underground drains for completion of biological decomposition. The solid part of the excreta (sludge) settles at the bottom. The sludge relies on natural decomposition. It is reduced in volume and is ultimately converted into inoffensive unstable product. However, the water carriage system is very expensive, technical and requires sewage treatment works. Now look at the non-water carriage system.</p>
<p>In this method, excreta are disposed of by deposition in a pit latrine. The pit latrine is the most important waste disposal method in the rural areas. In its simplest form, the pit latrine consists of the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>A hole in the ground</li>
<li>A squatting place for sitting or standing</li>
<li>A hut or shelter for privacy</li>
</ul>
<p>In this way the excreta is safe from fingers, feet, flies and food. Making a concrete slab, which is easier to wash and keep clean, should strengthen the squatting place. The hole should have a cover with a handle, which ensures that flies do not breed or get in and out of the latrine.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260116-da4297da.jpeg" alt="img-9.jpeg"></p>
<p>You need to consult your public health officer to give you more information on ventilated improved pit latrines, which are found in many villages.</p>
<p>These latrines feature vent pipes designed for controlling flies. You will have seen them in the community.</p>
<p>The main advantages of a pit latrine are:</p>
<ul>
<li>It does not require piped water supply</li>
<li>It is cheap to construct as the materials are locally available</li>
<li>The community does not need close supervision during the construction</li>
</ul>
<p>As already mentioned, there are various other types of pit latrines. The borehole latrine is bored into the ground about six metres deep and four metres in diameter instead of digging a pit. It has a smaller volume and fills up faster than a pit. It is faster to install, and is appropriate</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>following disasters where there is urgent need to install many latrines.</p>
<p>The trench latrine is a latrine where a trench is dug and a number of holes with dividing partitions constructed over it. These types of latrines are used in temporary work camps.</p>
<p>Bucket latrines are also known as pail closets and are used where the water tables are high. A squatting slab or seat is placed above the bucket, which is filled within a few days. Some of the negative aspects of this type of latrine are the unpleasant job of emptying it and the spillage, which attracts flies.</p>
<p>Finally, the composting pit latrine is suitable where the water table is too high for a deep pit latrine to be dug.</p>
<p>From this description of liquid waste disposal, you should now be in a position to assist the community to construct and use hygienic disposal methods.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="solid-waste-disposal">Solid Waste Disposal<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#solid-waste-disposal" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The amount and type of refuse produced varies from one community to another, as does the means of disposal. Usually, solid refuse disposal is not a problem in the rural areas except around shops, markets or other places where people aggregate. However, in big cities such as Nairobi, Kisumu and Mombasa, there is indiscriminate dumping of domestic and industrial refuse.</p>
<p>Health facilities, especially, should set a good example by employing hygienic methods of refuse disposal.</p>
<p>Refuse in towns should be stored in proper containers. These containers should be:</p>
<ul>
<li>Watertight plastic or metal with a tight-fitting lid or polythene bags</li>
<li>Rust resistant</li>
<li>Easily filled, emptied and cleaned</li>
<li>Have side handles</li>
<li>Rest on a concrete slab to ensure cleanliness of adjacent ground</li>
</ul>
<p>In towns collection should be regular, systematic and reliable. Specially constructed vehicles for this purpose can be found in big towns such as Nairobi, Kisumu, Nakuru and Mombasa.</p>
<p>In rural areas you should get the support of the village health committee and arrange for refuse to be collected and disposed of regularly, especially after market days. Simple methods of refuse collection should be encouraged in rural areas.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="advantages-of-proper-waste-disposal">Advantages of Proper Waste Disposal<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#advantages-of-proper-waste-disposal" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Proper solid waste disposal has several advantages. These include the prevention of:</p>
<ul>
<li>Breeding of pests and vectors</li>
<li>Foul smells</li>
<li>Contamination of water sources</li>
<li>Accidents from sharp objects</li>
<li>Overcrowding where space can be created for better utilisation</li>
</ul>
<p>The health department and municipalities are responsible for refuse disposal in towns. The choice of disposal method is determined by its cost. In the rural areas the health worker and the village health committee are responsible for refuse disposal in individual houses, shops, hotels and markets.</p>
<p>How does your family and community store and collect their refuse and how can these methods be improved?</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="dumping">Dumping<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dumping" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This can be in the sea or river. In Kenya, this method is most often used in the towns along the coast. This becomes a health hazard and the littering of the shoreline is an unpleasant sight. Another commonly used method is open dumping, which should be discouraged. Open dumps provide breeding places for rats, mosquitoes and flies.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="burning">Burning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#burning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This may be done in a number of ways. These include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Simple open air burning</li>
<li>Burning in a trench</li>
<li>Using a simple mud-brick incinerator</li>
</ul>
<p>The open burning of combustible refuse is frequently used but it is not very effective. This method often leaves tins and broken bottles littering the surrounding area. This can cause accidents, especially to children. The smoke and odour contribute to air pollution. There is a fire risk and the rubbish sprawls all over while awaiting burning. It may become a breeding place for rodents and insect vectors.</p>
<p>Incinerators are an improved way of burning combustible refuse. Incinerators can be simple and cheap, or complex and expensive. Among the cheap ones is the bin incinerator made out of a drum with fire bars across it and air holes underneath. A more expensive one is built out of</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>brick and fitted with chimneys. These incinerators allow more complete combustion and produce less smoke. Most hospitals use incinerators.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="composting">Composting<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#composting" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Composting is "a process in which, under suitable environmental conditions aerobic micro-organisms break down organic matter to fairly stable humus" (A. D. Luca and H.M. Gilles, 2003). The decomposition process occurs naturally on the ground when droppings from the trees and animals are converted by micro-organisms to humus. Aerobic composting is normally odour free.</p>
<p>This method is, cheap, convenient and recommended especially in rural areas. Wet and dry refuse is heaped in alternative layers on to a plot about 2.5 square metres to a depth of about 1.5 square metres. The refuse is then covered with grass and earth. Compost requires frequent turning after 30 days then after 60 days. This turning helps to distribute all parts of the heap to undergo the high temperature of the interior. After 90 days the refuse is ready to be used as manure.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="controlled-tipping">Controlled Tipping<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#controlled-tipping" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This method involves depositing refuse into depressions or large holes in the ground. These tips should be situated at least half a kilometre away from settlement, preferably out of sight and down wind. This is an effective method for hygienic disposal of refuse. It can be used where sufficient land is available. The method consists of three steps as illustrated in the diagram on your right.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="recycling">Recycling<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#recycling" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a method of re-using non-biodegradable refuse such as paper, bottles, plastics, metal cans and so on. Although it requires special processes to render the items suitable for reuse, it is a method that should be encouraged.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260116-36690fe5.jpeg" alt="img-10.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="section-3-appropriate-methods-of-handling-food">SECTION 3: APPROPRIATE METHODS OF HANDLING FOOD<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-3-appropriate-methods-of-handling-food" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Welcome to section three of this unit. In this section you will cover food and principles of food hygiene. Food is essential for growth, development and in the provision of energy. However, food could also be responsible for the spread of some diseases. The aim of food hygiene is to prevent the contamination of food at any stage.</p>
<p>These stages are production, collection, storage, sale, preparation and consumption.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="objectives">Objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>By the end of this section you will be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Describe the sources of food</li>
<li>Describe methods of food storage</li>
<li>Describe preparation and preservation of food</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="sources-of-food">Sources of Food<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sources-of-food" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Sources of food vary widely. They include rearing, feeding, marketing, crop production and slaughter of animals. Foods that are of animal origin should only be derived from animals that are legally allowed for human consumption, for example, some countries ban game meat. Meanwhile, crop production should follow rules in agricultural practice, which involve spraying crops against pests. Farmers are advised on safe use of pesticides.</p>
<p>During food processing certain standards of food hygiene are applied, for example, in milk treatment, drinks and tinned foods. The chemicals used as preservatives are also regulated for the safety of the consumers. The slaughter of animals is governed by several rules and acts, for example, the Meat Control Act, the Veterinary Act and the Public Health Act.</p>
<p>Food can be contaminated by excreta, dirty fingers, flies, poisonous insecticides or pesticides on vegetables or chemical preservation of food. It can also be contaminated if it is derived from infected</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>animals, for example, animals with tapeworms or brucellosis.</p>
<p>You will now look at the recommended conditions for storing different types of food.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="food-storage">Food Storage<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#food-storage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Storage will depend on the type and packaging of the food.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="dry-foods">Dry Foods<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dry-foods" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>These include foods like maize, beans, and wheat (cereals). Such foods should be stored in dry, airy conditions in improved granaries.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="bagged-foods">Bagged Foods<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#bagged-foods" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>These foods should be stored on raised shelves at least 18 inches above the floor or ground level. This enables the store to be swept and washed easily. It also allows for easy inspection for pest detection.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="perishable-foods">Perishable Foods<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#perishable-foods" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>These are foods that go bad within a short time. Such foods include dairy products, meat and fish. They should be refrigerated to inhibit the multiplication of bacteria.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="food-preservation">Food Preservation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#food-preservation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is defined as any method used to treat food for the purpose of prolonging its life without appreciable loss of its quality and appeal. Most human food is of biological origin and there is continuous metabolism to produce the end product. This applies to food of both animal and plant origin, for example, meat, milk, fish, leaves, tubers and seeds. When an animal or plant dies, they lose the mechanism of protection from bacteria, fungi and moulds.</p>
<p>Thus, you preserve food in order to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Increase its shelf-life, for example, canned foods</li>
<li>Render the food safe for consumption, for example, highly perishable foods like milk</li>
<li>Conserve the food for use during the periods of scarcity, for instance, dried cereals and vegetables</li>
<li>Avail seasonal foods, like fruits, throughout the year</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="principles-of-food-preservation">Principles of Food Preservation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#principles-of-food-preservation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are two principles of food preservation.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="principle-1">Principle 1<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#principle-1" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Destroy organisms responsible for spoilage through heat treatment.</p>
