<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="principle-2">Principle 2<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#principle-2" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Inhibit the micro-organisms through cold treatment.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="more-information">more information.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#more-information" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="moulds">Moulds<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#moulds" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Affect the surfaces of foods containing high sugar and salt. They also affect dry foods that may become damp due to poor storage.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="yeasts">Yeasts<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#yeasts" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Affect foods that have acid or sugar in high concentration, for example, dried fruits, and concentrated fruit juices.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="bacteria">Bacteria<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#bacteria" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Affect foods under various conditions apart from dry food.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="heat-treatment">Heat Treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#heat-treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The following are methods of destroying organisms through heat treatment.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cooking">Cooking<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cooking" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a heating process, which aims to produce more palatable food. Cooked food generally keeps longer than raw foods as long as recontamination is minimised. Cooking destroys or reduces micro-organisms and potential toxins in food. Cooking also inactivates undesirable enzymes in food. It alters the colour, texture and flavour and improves the digestibility of food. On the other hand, cooking may cause degradation of food nutrients, for example, over cooking vegetables destroys vitamin C.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="blanching">Blanching<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#blanching" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is the process where most vegetable foods are heat treated at <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>70</mn><mo>âˆ’</mo><msup><mn>100</mn><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">âˆ˜</mo></msup><mi mathvariant="normal">C</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">70 - 100^{\circ}\mathrm{C}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7278em; vertical-align: -0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord">70</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">âˆ’</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord">10</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">0</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.6741em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">âˆ˜</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mord mathrm">C</span></span></span></span></span> for 2 - 10 minutes. This is done by immersing food in boiling water</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>or exposing it to steam. Blanching is used before freezing, canning or drying. This process inactivates enzymes, drives out air bubbles trapped in food, enhances retention of green colours and reduces micro-organisms.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pasteurisation">Pasteurisation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pasteurisation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a relatively slow method of heat treatment. Pasteurisation is generally carried out at a temperature of below 100Â°C. This method is used to increase the life span of the product. This method reduces organisms that cause spoilage and eliminates pathogens.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sterilisation">Sterilisation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sterilisation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In this method heat is used to kill all micro-organisms and their spores at a temperature of above 100Â°C. The sterilised food must be stored in an airtight container to prevent the entry of and recontamination by micro-organisms.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="canning">Canning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#canning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In this method, the food is first heated at a temperature that kills all bacteria and it is then sealed up in sterile cans or bottles. This prevents bacteria from getting into it and enables it to remain safe for a long time at room temperature.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cold-treatment-and-other-methods">Cold Treatment and Other Methods<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cold-treatment-and-other-methods" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="freezing">Freezing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#freezing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>This is the most satisfactory method currently available for long-term preservation of food. When properly done, freezing is effective for retaining the colour, texture, flavour and nutritive value. Food must be deep-frozen at 0-4Â°C to remain palatable. This keeps food fresh for weeks or months.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="salting">Salting<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#salting" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>This is the saturation of food with salt or sugar, for example, ham, jam and jelly. The added solute reduces microbial activity due to its dehydrating effect. The salt and sugar solutions are more concentrated than the cytoplasm inside the cell. Therefore, the water passes out of the cell into the concentrate, dehydrating the cell.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="smoking-and-drying">Smoking and Drying<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#smoking-and-drying" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Drying and smoking makes food unsuitable for the bacteria to grow and multiply. Fish or meat may be preserved by these methods. A wood rack is made and fish or meat is placed on it. A wood fire, which generates heat and thick smoke, is made under the rack. The heat will dry the fish or meat, and the smoke gets inside the food to act as a preservative. Green vegetables, cereals and legumes can be preserved by drying them in the sun. If food is preserved by drying, it must be stored in a dry place until it is used.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="food-safety">Food Safety<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#food-safety" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="preparation-of-food">Preparation of Food<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#preparation-of-food" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Adequate personal hygiene must be observed when preparing food in order to prevent disease.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="health">Health<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#health" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Individuals suffering from respiratory infections such as colds or sore throat should not work with food until they get well. This also applies to people with infected cuts, skin eruptions and diarrhoeal diseases like dysentery and typhoid.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="clothing">Clothing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clothing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Individuals working with food should wear clean washable outer garments. Every worker in the kitchen or washing dishes should wear a clean uniform or apron. These clothes should be worn when the worker is in the premises where food preparation is taking place. This avoids cross-food contamination.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="head-covering">Head Covering<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#head-covering" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>To avoid hair from getting into food, hair bands, caps or nets should be used to cover the head when handling food.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="personal-hygiene">Personal Hygiene<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#personal-hygiene" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>A daily bath is necessary for every individual. Wash hands before handling the food, use clean utensils and avoid habits such as nose picking. Nails should be kept short and clean.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="food">Food<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#food" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Raw food should be separated from cooked food. All vegetables should be cleaned</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>thoroughly before preparation for cooking. Fruits should be washed before eating. The food should be hygienically prepared and cooked adequately. All food utensils should be cleaned properly after use and left to dry before being stored in a clean place</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="environment">Environment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#environment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The environment pertaining to the preparation of food should be clean throughout. The area should be dust free. This includes the floors and all the surfaces used for food preparation. The facility itself should be clean and with adequate ventilation and lighting.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="common-food-borne-diseases-and-their-causes">Common Food Borne Diseases and Their Causes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#common-food-borne-diseases-and-their-causes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>Disease</th><th>Cause</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Illness affecting the mental function</td><td>Some naturally poisonous plants</td></tr><tr><td>Poisoning</td><td>Chemicals such as lead, arsenic</td></tr><tr><td>Ascariasis</td><td>Parasites e.g.</td></tr><tr><td>Taeniasis</td><td>Askaris lumbricoides</td></tr><tr><td>Amoebiasis</td><td>Taenia solium/sagnata</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>Entamoeba histolytica</td></tr><tr><td>Typhoid fever</td><td>Salmonella typhi</td></tr><tr><td>Paratyphoid fever</td><td>Salmonella paratyphi</td></tr><tr><td>Food poisoning</td><td>Salmonella typhiniurium</td></tr><tr><td>Bacillary dysentery</td><td>Shigella</td></tr><tr><td>Military Tuberculosis</td><td>Bovine tuberculosis</td></tr><tr><td>Brucellosis</td><td>Brucella</td></tr><tr><td>Cholera</td><td>Vibrio cholera</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="food-safety-regulations">Food Safety Regulations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#food-safety-regulations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The safety of food is so important that our government has passed laws to protect the public. These laws cover many aspects of food handling and health officers are generally responsible for enforcing these laws. Agricultural personnel assist them, where necessary.</p>
<p>You will look at some of the factors that should be considered when preparing or handling food and some of the food-borne diseases.</p>
<p><strong>Remember:</strong></p>
<p>The Public Health Act Cap 242 is an Act of Parliament to make provision for securing and maintaining health. This act is divided into 15 parts. Each part deals with a specific aspect of public health.</p>
<p>Part 10 of the Act deals 'with protection of foodstuffs'. This part regulates the construction of buildings used for storage of foodstuffs. Secondly, it prohibits residing or sleeping in kitchens or food stores.</p>
<p>Part (II) deals with 'milk, meat and other articles of food'. This part prohibits the sale of unwholesome foods. It gives powers to authorised officers to inspect and examine food, seize and recommend disposal at any time. These laws aim at protecting the public and the public health officers are responsible for enforcing them. As a community health nurse you need to work closely with public health officers to apply the food safety regulations.</p>
<p>The following are some of the areas that need close supervision.</p>
<p><strong>Meat</strong></p>
<p>Meat is one of the commonest foods that cause problems to the public. Therefore, it is important</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>that inspection of slaughterhouses, cows, sheep, goats and pigs be carried out. The same case applies to butcheries where meat is sold.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="milk">Milk<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#milk" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Milk is one of the foods that are easily contaminated and cause problems to the public. Inspection of shops where milk is sold is of paramount importance. The milk should be safe and clean. It should be obtained from healthy cows as it can transmit bovine tuberculosis among other diseases. The room for handling milk should be clean, dustless and separate from the barn. The pails, cans, bottles, coolers and other equipment, which comes into contact with the milk, should be thoroughly cleaned.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="homes">Homes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#homes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is the responsibility of the community health nurse to share health messages with community members on food hygiene. These include maintenance of personal hygiene as covered earlier, that is cleaning the utensils, handling them with clean hands, and storing them in clean and dry cupboards or containers.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="farms">Farms<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#farms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The community should follow the regulations on the use of insecticides and pesticides in form of sprays and fertilizers. This will help them to use each of them correctly depending on the age of the crop. Your role as a community health nurse is to encourage the community to adhere to the instructions from the agricultural field educators. Moreover, instructions are given on the respective containers of these pesticides. You should teach the community about regulations of food storage and preservation of different types of food. The harvest should be carried out when the crops are completely ripe or ready to facilitate longer preservation. The cereals and legumes should be dried properly before storage to avoid spoilage. All perishable foods should be consumed at the right time.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="markets">Markets<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#markets" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>All types of foodstuffs are sold in markets. The markets should be designed in a manner that considers stations where similar types of food should be stored and sold, for example, vegetables of all kinds, dry foods like cereals, fruits and cooked foods. The market should be kept clean and proper refuse disposal maintained. The food sold should be clean and fit for human consumption. This, therefore, explains the importance of inspecting markets by public health officers. These officers have the power to close markets and condemn foods to prevent disease outbreaks.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="hotels">Hotels<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hotels" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Hotels, restaurants and food shops should also be inspected under hygiene regulations. They require regular inspection by the public health officers. All the food handlers should be supervised and a regular medical examination is mandatory for them to prevent spread of diseases through food handling. Licenses should only be given to hotel owners who have met the requirements. Laboratory examinations may be necessary for food such as pre-cooked meat. The use of uniforms, aprons, head coverings, as described earlier, should be observed in the hotels. Proper personal and environmental hygiene in the hotel premises should be maintained.</p>
<p>The hotel should store, preserve, prepare, cook and serve the food according to public health regulations. The law also empowers closure of hotels which do not meet the regulations.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 85 of 267
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 86 of 267
Bishop's Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="section-4-housing">SECTION 4: HOUSING<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-4-housing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The provision of good housing is an essential aspect of environmental health. Good housing is a requirement for every human being because it provides shelter and protection from environmental hazards.</p>
<p>Think of some health problems that would be associated with the following poor housing conditions:</p>
<ul>
<li>Overcrowding and poor ventilation</li>
<li>Unscreened windows</li>
<li>Cooking fires on the floor</li>
<li>Earth walls and dirty floors</li>
</ul>
<table><thead><tr><th>Housing Condition</th><th>Health Risk</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Overcrowding and poor ventilation</td><td>Airborne droplet infections</td></tr><tr><td>Unscreened windows</td><td>Malaria</td></tr><tr><td>Cooking fires on the floor</td><td>Accidents and burns in children</td></tr><tr><td>Earth walls and dirty floors</td><td>Breeding of flies and bedbugs</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>A combination of dampness, lack of light, poor ventilation and overcrowding will contribute to the spread of airborne and droplet infections.</p>
<p>Earth floors and walls permit the entry and breeding of flies and bedbugs, while unscreened windows permit entry of mosquitoes.</p>
<p>Cooking fires on the floor are hazards to small children. Inadequate space to talk and play, especially in town houses, is one of the reasons why fathers and children leave home thereby adding to social problems.</p>
<p>For these reasons it is important to improve the quality of housing. You can help your community live in safe houses, by making simple improvements using locally available materials.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="objectives">Objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>By the end of this section you will be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Describe the types of houses</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Describe the criteria for an adequate house</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Describe a suitable building site</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Describe the characteristics of poor housing</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Describe how you would involve the community in improving housing</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="types-of-housing">Types of Housing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-housing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A house can be permanent, semi-permanent or temporary.</p>
<p>These structures will be considered in turn.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="permanent-houses">Permanent Houses<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#permanent-houses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This type of house has a stone foundation, a cemented floor and plastered walls. The roof is covered with iron sheets, tiles or stones in the case of flats or maisonettes. This type of house has advantages in that it is easy to keep the floor and walls clean. However, the floor should be kept dry to avoid accidental falls. Permanent houses are not cheap to construct and it is necessary to budget for the activity.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="semi-permanent-houses">Semi-Permanent Houses<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#semi-permanent-houses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a type of house whereby the floor is usually cemented but does not necessarily have a stone foundation. The walls are made of iron sheets or sometimes timber. The house is iron roofed. If you work in a rural community then you must have come across this type of a house. It is satisfactory and easy to keep clean. However, appropriate preservatives for timbers have to be used or else termites destroy it. In many places mud bricks are used and they are an appropriate method of improving houses. Since it is less expensive than a permanent house, you have the responsibility of encouraging members of the community to try and acquire at least this type of a house.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="temporary-houses">Temporary Houses<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#temporary-houses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This type of house may be found in rural and slums areas. The floor is earthen, the walls are made of cardboard, polythene paper, grass or mud. The roof is thatched with the same</p>
<p>material as the walls. This type of a house does not provide for privacy and can easily catch fire. Temporary houses are a health hazard and do not meet the requirements for good housing. They should be discouraged as much as possible</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="criteria-for-an-adequate-house">Criteria for an Adequate House<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#criteria-for-an-adequate-house" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A good house should meet biological, physical and social criteria.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="biological-criteria">Biological Criteria<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#biological-criteria" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Good housing minimises the risk of transmission of diseases. The spread of gastro-intestinal infections is minimised by some important factors. These include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Good water supply</li>
<li>Good food storage, preservation and preparation</li>
<li>Adequate facilities for washing utensils and well designed kitchens</li>
<li>Adequate methods of refuse disposal</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="physical-criteria">Physical Criteria<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#physical-criteria" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The house should be safe for every occupant. This means that home accidents should be prevented. It is, therefore, necessary that appropriate safety devices be provided for. The house should also be free from air pollution.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="social-criteria">Social Criteria<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#social-criteria" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Good housing should be designed to enable the family function effectively in regard to its cultural background. This means that the required privacy for adults should be catered for. It should have a suitable setting for bringing up children.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="characteristics-of-adequate-housing">Characteristics of Adequate Housing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#characteristics-of-adequate-housing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The following are the characteristics of a good house.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="natural-light">Natural Light<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#natural-light" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The sun provides natural light, which is essential for physical growth, especially in young children. Lighting is also essential for proper vision. The presence of sunlight into the house kills some micro-organisms. This underscores the need for sunlight in the house. Some insects are also driven away by adequate lighting.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="artificial-lighting">Artificial Lighting<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#artificial-lighting" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This type of lighting is needed at night. The sources are electricity, oil lamps and gas. The type of lighting used should correspond to the purpose for which it is needed in the house.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="ventilation">Ventilation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ventilation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Fresh air is necessary for our health. Ventilation of a house is the removal of impure air and pouring in pure air. This is achieved through windows and door ventilators. Good ventilation in the house is important, because it keeps the air on continuous movement without creating draught, cools the housing and maintains the room temperature at a constant.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="room-separation">Room Separation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#room-separation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The house should have adequate rooms to provide separate accommodation for adults and children. The shelter for animals should be separate from the main house. There should also be separate rooms for food storage and preparation.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="others">Others<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#others" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The house should have, where possible, cemented floor and plastered walls to protect against insects and should be rodent-proof. It should also have water supply in adequate and reliable quantity and quality. It should have a good latrine and a clean compound. It should be equipped with proper methods of refuse disposal, for example, composting, burning or burying waste. The house should be dry. The cooking arrangements should be satisfactory to</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>avoid home accidents. Generally, there should be an effort to protect against all types of home accidents, for instance, those caused by fire, tools and chemicals.</p>
<p><strong>Remember:</strong>
It may not always be possible to meet all the necessary requirements for adequate housing. However, housing can be improved in a number of simple and practical ways.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="suitable-building-sites">Suitable Building Sites<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#suitable-building-sites" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The following factors should be considered when selecting a suitable site for a house:</p>
<ul>
<li>The soil should be suitable for construction.</li>
<li>The site should be dry, sunny and exposed to free air.</li>
<li>The surroundings should be hygienic and healthy.</li>
<li>The site should be away from noisy factories, cinema halls and heavy traffic.</li>
<li>It should be on high ground to avoid water from standing and stagnating. This will prevent breeding of mosquitoes.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="characteristics-of-poor-housing">Characteristics of Poor Housing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#characteristics-of-poor-housing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A poor house does not protect its inhabitants from environmental hazards. It may have some or all the following negative characteristics:</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="characteristics">Characteristics<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#characteristics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Dampness due to poor drainage.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Overcrowding is a common feature in poor housing. This is due to an insufficient number of rooms. Dampness and overcrowding enhance the spread of common respiratory diseases such as colds, influenza, tuberculosis and pneumonia.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Earthen floors and walls encourage breeding of fleas and bed bugs while unscreened windows encourage entry of mosquitoes.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Unprotected fire places with poor cooking arrangements cause home accidents with children. Working tools can cause accidents if not properly stored.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Water supply and storage, which lacks hygiene, poses a health hazard for the transmission of water-borne diseases.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Proper storage of clean utensils is often lacking in poor housing. This is accompanied by poor personal hygiene in the preparation and serving of food.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The home environment may lack a good latrine, usually accompanied by improper excreta and inadequate refuse disposal. This increases the chances of getting hookworm infestation.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Compounds with tall grass, pools of water and sprawling litter may provide good breeding places for mosquitoes, rodents and other vectors responsible for transmission of many communicable diseases.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="community-involvement-in-improving-housing">Community Involvement in Improving Housing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#community-involvement-in-improving-housing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is very important to explain to the community the reasons they need to adopt new hygienic practices. If the members of the community are not well convinced, your environmental health measures will fail. This is because new practices mean a change in people's behaviour and they will not be willing to change unless they see personal advantages in it. Avoiding diseases, making more money or just being more comfortable are some of the advantages that must be emphasised to the community. You must make the new idea attractive. The following are only some ways of how to introduce change.</p>
<ul>
<li>Find out what people think about the problem. Do they see it as a problem? If they do not, then you will have to help them understand that the problem exists and needs to be given attention.</li>
<li>Encourage them to think of possible solutions and guide them towards those that are technically possible and suitable for the situation. Encourage community participation.</li>
<li>Aim to set an example in your health facility or home.</li>
<li>Talk and work with people, encourage them to ask for advice or help in solving their problems, for example, inadequate water supplies, waste disposal, food safety regulations and hygiene,</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>improved housing, controlling of vectors and pests.</p>
<p>The community would enjoy living in good housing. A little effort is needed to improve housing by using locally available resources.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sensitisation">Sensitisation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sensitisation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Sensitisation is the process of creating awareness. Community health nurses come in contact with the communities and should make use of these opportunities to share health messages with them. You should start at the health facility then extend your efforts to their homes. The health team will have conducted a community diagnosis so as to have valid information on the problem.</p>
<p>The following steps can be followed when trying to involve the community.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="meeting-the-health-team-members">Meeting the Health Team Members<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#meeting-the-health-team-members" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The first step involves planning to meet and explain the need for community involvement, with the health team members. Ensure that the relevant consultants and government officers dealing with housing are invited so that they can give pertinent information on housing matters according to the Housing Act. In this meeting, the health team members will deliberate on community sensitisation and identify ways of improving housing in the community. All the health team members should be committed to carrying out their plans for solving the housing problem.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sharing-health-messages-daily-at-the-health-facility-about-improving-housing">Sharing Health Messages Daily at the Health Facility about Improving Housing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sharing-health-messages-daily-at-the-health-facility-about-improving-housing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The second step will be to start sensitising the community at the primary health care facility. This will be accomplished by sharing health messages on improved housing. In this way, the patients and clients will get pertinent information on types of houses, criteria for adequate housing, effects of housing on health, characteristics of poor housing and diseases associated with poor housing. This will make the</p>
<p>community aware of the problem and the need to improve housing for the family.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="meeting-the-community-leaders">Meeting the Community Leaders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#meeting-the-community-leaders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The third step is where the community health nurse organises to meet and go over the subject with the community leaders of the area. These leaders include formal leaders in government offices, for example, the District Commissioner, the District Officer, Chief and Assistant Chief. The informal leaders, such as opinion leaders, community own resource persons, leaders of women, men and youth groups should also be involved. Moreover, you should target community-based health workers, traditional birth attendants and community-based distributors of family planning. These leaders will be aware of the problem and the need for improved housing in their community. They will identify and suggest ways of improvement. You should be able to guide them on the techniques of carrying out the health activities. You may use clinical records to confirm the health problem and the need for community involvement.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="identifying-ways-of-improvement">Identifying Ways of Improvement<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#identifying-ways-of-improvement" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Through the previously-mentioned meetings and activities, the health team and the community leaders will identify many ways of improving housing. From their list they will select the best alternative and then plan and organise their resources, that is, manpower, money, materials, and time to carry out the selected activities. Some of these activities will be the provision of outreach clinic services. During the clinic session, the same content on improved housing will be covered in the health messages.</p>
<p>During home visits, the nurse, public health technician and community-based health worker should inspect the houses and focus on simple practical ways of improvement. This will enhance the implementation as the solutions are being provided directly at home.</p>
<p>A school health service is another community health activity where this knowledge may be imparted for the children to share with their parents. The community health nurse, with her team members, conducts regular supervisory visits to the centres of community-based health care activities. These supportive visits help the</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>groups to build their self-confidence and improve their skills. They are encouraged to explore solutions to their housing problems. They also encourage mutual respect and understanding between the health team and community members.</p>
<p>The effectiveness of these health activities will be determined on monthly basis when outreach and school health services are carried out. It is necessary to let the community know the time frame for evaluation of the activity. A period of about six months would be appropriate.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="evaluation-of-housing-activities">Evaluation of Housing Activities<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#evaluation-of-housing-activities" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>After the implementation of the housing activities it will be necessary to evaluate the extent of community participation. Community participation builds the confidence of the community members. It enables the members to examine their situation.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="remember">Remember:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#remember" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Community participation was covered in unit two of this module.</p>
<p>You are able to obtain information from reports on home visiting, outreach clinic services, also from the public health technician and community-based health workers. The reports can be gathered from the community's formal leaders.</p>
<p>The Ministry of Housing will also give their reports.</p>
<p>Finally, the patients and clients will also be interviewed on improved housing. It will be necessary for the nurse to carry out a community survey in the area to assess the community participation. This will be carried out at the time suggested for evaluation. The questionnaire will include all the necessary aspects of housing and focusing on new improvements. The findings of this survey will be communicated to the community leaders and the community. This will enable the community to take appropriate action.</p>

<p>SECTION 5: CONTROL OF VECTORS AND PESTS</p>
<p>Introduction</p>
<p>This is the final section of unit three.</p>
<p>In this section you will learn about vectors and pests.</p>
<p>Objectives</p>
<p>By the end of this section you will be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Describe diseases associated with vectors and pests</li>
<li>Describe methods of control of vectors and pests</li>
<li>Describe how you will involve the community in the control process</li>
</ul>
<p>Diseases Associated With Vectors</p>
<p>A vector is an organism, usually an insect, which transmits a pathogen from a source of infection to a susceptible host. Insects are controlled because of the role they play in disease transmission, destruction of food and building materials. To control vectors you have to deprive them of suitable breeding places, food and harbour.</p>
<p>ways a vector may transmit pathogens.</p>
<p>Mechanical Transmission</p>
<p>In this mode of transmission, the vector carries the infective pathogen or agent on its body or limbs. Alternatively, the infective agent may be ingested by the vector and excreted unchanged in its faeces.</p>
<p>Biological Transmission</p>
<p>The vector acquires the infective agent from the blood or skin tissue of the infected host and the infective organism undergoes some development in the vector. The infective vector may also inoculate the infective agent from its salivary secretion into a new host to cause disease, for example, in the transmission of malaria.</p>
<p>Contamination of Skin or Mucous Membranes</p>
<p>The host may be infected through contamination of skin or mucous membranes by the infective faeces of the vector, for example, louse borne relapsing fever.</p>
<p>Ingestion</p>
<p>The host may acquire infection by ingesting the vector, for example, guinea worm.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 91 of 267
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>List six vectors and the diseases they transmit.</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Vector</th><th>Disease Transmitted</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Houseflies</td><td>1. Amoebic and bacillary dysentery</td></tr></tbody></table>
